	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Slavs</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavic_countries&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic countries">Slavic countries</a>)</span></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Early Slavs</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Slav" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Slav_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Slav (disambiguation)">Slav (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slavic_World_updated.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Slavic_World_updated.png/325px-Slavic_World_updated.png" decoding="async" width="325" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Slavic_World_updated.png/488px-Slavic_World_updated.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Slavic_World_updated.png/650px-Slavic_World_updated.png 2x" data-file-width="6460" data-file-height="3480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Slavic_World_updated.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World map of countries with: <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Majority Slavic ethnicities</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #22B14C; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Minority Slavic populations (&gt;10%)</div></div></div></div>
<p><b>Slavs</b> are <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> people who speak the various <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic languages</a> of the larger <a href="/wiki/Balto-Slavic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Balto-Slavic language">Balto-Slavic linguistic</a> group. They are native to <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, stretching from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeastern</a> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> all the way north and eastwards to <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northeast Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">Northern Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> (especially <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Kazakhstan" title="Russians in Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Turkmenistan" title="Russians in Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>), as well as historically in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> (particularly in Eastern Germany) and <a href="/wiki/West_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="West Asia">Western Asia</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>). From the early 6th century they spread to inhabit the majority of Central, Eastern and Southeastern Europe. Today, there is a large Slavic diaspora throughout <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Slavic_Americans" title="Slavic Americans">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> as a result of <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-msu_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msu-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Slavs are the largest ethno-linguistic group in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarford20011_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarford20011-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples_(modern)" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic peoples (modern)">Germanic peoples</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance peoples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pop_1996_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pop_1996-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Present-day Slavic people are classified into <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a> (chiefly <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">Rusyns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>), <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a> (chiefly <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashubians" title="Kashubians">Kashubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moravians" title="Moravians">Moravians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesians" title="Silesians">Silesians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorbs" title="Sorbs">Sorbs</a>), and <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a> (chiefly <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="Macedonians (ethnic group)">Macedonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins" title="Montenegrins">Montenegrins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenes" title="Slovenes">Slovenes</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Slav_(people)_-_Britannica_Online_Encyclopedia_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slav_(people)_-_Britannica_Online_Encyclopedia-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-palgrave_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palgrave-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPotSN_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPotSN-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-belgrade_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belgrade-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Slavs can be further grouped by religion. <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Orthodox Christianity</a> is practiced by the majority of Slavs. The <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Slavs" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Slavs">Orthodox Slavs</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group)" title="Macedonians (ethnic group)">Macedonians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegrins" title="Montenegrins">Montenegrins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">Rusyns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> and are defined by Orthodox customs and <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic script</a>, as well as their cultural connection to the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> (<a href="/wiki/Montenegrins" title="Montenegrins">Montenegrins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> also use <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> on equal terms). Their second most common religion is <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Slavic_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic Catholic">Catholic Slavs</a> include <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashubians" title="Kashubians">Kashubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moravians" title="Moravians">Moravians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesians" title="Silesians">Silesians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenes" title="Slovenes">Slovenes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sorbs" title="Sorbs">Sorbs</a> and are defined by their <a href="/wiki/Latinate" class="mw-redirect" title="Latinate">Latinate</a> influence and heritage and connection to <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>. There are also substantial <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> minorities, especially among the <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a>, such as the historical <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemian</a> (Czech) <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">Hussites</a>.
</p><p>The second-largest religion among the Slavs after Christianity is <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Slavs" title="Muslim Slavs">Muslim Slavs</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosniaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pomaks" title="Pomaks">Pomaks</a> (Bulgarian Muslims), <a href="/wiki/Gorani_people" title="Gorani people">Gorani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torbe%C5%A1i" class="mw-redirect" title="Torbeši">Torbeši</a> (Macedonian Muslims), and other <a href="/wiki/Muslims_(nationality)" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims (nationality)">Muslims of the former Yugoslavia</a>. Modern Slavic nations and ethnic groups are considerably diverse both genetically and culturally, and relations between them – even within the individual groups – range from ethnic solidarity to mutual hostility.<sup id="cite_ref-Psychology_Press_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Psychology_Press-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnonym">Ethnonym</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ethnonym">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Slavs_(ethnonym)" title="Slavs (ethnonym)">Slavs (ethnonym)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg/220px-%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg/330px-%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg/440px-%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2020" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%8F%D0%BD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boyan_(bard)" title="Boyan (bard)">Boyan</a>, a legendary story teller and oral historian</div></div></div>
<p>The oldest mention of the Slavic ethnonym is the 6th century AD <a href="/wiki/Procopius" title="Procopius">Procopius</a>, writing in <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greek" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Greek">Byzantine Greek</a>, using various forms such as <i>Sklaboi</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Σκλάβοι</span>), <i>Sklabēnoi</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Σκλαβηνοί</span>), <i>Sklauenoi</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Σκλαυηνοί</span>), <i>Sthlabenoi</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Σθλαβηνοί</span>), or  <i>Sklabinoi</i> (<span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Σκλαβῖνοι</span>),<sup id="cite_ref-procopius_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-procopius-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> while his contemporary <a href="/wiki/Jordanes" title="Jordanes">Jordanes</a> refers to the <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">Sclaveni</i> in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jordanes_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jordanes-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The oldest documents written in <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a>, dating from the 9th century, attest the autonym as <i>Slověne</i> (<span lang="cu" title="Church Slavonic language text">Словѣне</span>). These forms point back to a Slavic <a href="/wiki/Endonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Endonym">autonym</a> which can be reconstructed in <a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Slavic language">Proto-Slavic</a> as <span lang="sla-pro"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Slavic/slov%C4%9Bnin%D1%8A#Proto-Slavic" class="extiw" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Slavic/slověninъ">*Slověninъ</a></span>, plural <i>Slověne</i>.
</p><p>The reconstructed autonym &#42;<span lang="sla" title="Slavic languages collective text">Slověninъ</span> is usually considered a derivation from <i>slovo</i> ("word"), originally denoting "people who speak (the same language)", i.&#160;e. people who understand each other, in contrast to the Slavic word denoting German people, namely <span lang="sla-pro"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Slavic/n%C4%9Bm%D1%8Cc%D1%8C#Proto-Slavic" class="extiw" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Slavic/němьcь">*němьcь</a></span>, meaning "silent, mute people" (from Slavic <span lang="sla-pro"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Slavic/n%C4%9Bm%D1%8A#Proto-Slavic" class="extiw" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Slavic/němъ">*němъ</a></span> "<a href="/wiki/Muteness" title="Muteness">mute</a>, mumbling"). The word <i>slovo</i> ("word") and the related <i>slava</i> ("glory, fame") and <i>slukh</i> ("hearing") originate from the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a> root <i lang="ine-x-proto"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/%E1%B8%B1lew-#Proto-Indo-European" class="extiw" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/ḱlew-">*ḱlew-</a></i> ("be spoken of, glory"), cognate with Ancient Greek <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">κλέος</span> (<span title="Ancient Greek transliteration" lang="grc-Latn"><i>kléos</i></span> "fame"), as in the name <a href="/wiki/Pericles" title="Pericles">Pericles</a>, Latin <i lang="la"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/clueo#Latin" class="extiw" title="wikt:clueo">clueo</a></i> ("be called"), and English <i lang="en"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/loud#English" class="extiw" title="wikt:loud">loud</a></i>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_mentions">First mentions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First mentions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Early Slavs</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Veneti" title="Vistula Veneti">Vistula Veneti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spori" class="mw-redirect" title="Spori">Spori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antes_(people)" title="Antes (people)">Antes (people)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sclaveni" title="Sclaveni">Sclaveni</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wends" title="Wends">Wends</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png/220px-The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png/330px-The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="301" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_origin_and_dispersion_of_Slavs_in_the_5-10th_centuries.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The origin and migration of Slavs in Europe between the 5th and 10th centuries AD</div></div></div>
<p>Ancient Roman sources refer to the <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Early Slavic</a> peoples as <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Veneti" title="Vistula Veneti">Veneti</a>, who dwelt in a region of central Europe east of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_Peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic Peoples">Germanic</a> tribe of <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>, and west of the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatians</a> in the 1st and 2nd centuries AD.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The Slavs under name of the <i><a href="/wiki/Antes_(people)" title="Antes (people)">Antes</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Sclaveni" title="Sclaveni">Sclaveni</a></i> first appear in <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> records in the early 6th century. Byzantine historiographers under emperor <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian I</a> (527–565), such as <a href="/wiki/Procopius_of_Caesarea" class="mw-redirect" title="Procopius of Caesarea">Procopius of Caesarea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordanes" title="Jordanes">Jordanes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theophylact_Simocatta" title="Theophylact Simocatta">Theophylact Simocatta</a> describe tribes of these names emerging from the area of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>, the lower <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, invading the Danubian provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Empire">Eastern Empire</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jordanes" title="Jordanes">Jordanes</a>, in his work <i><a href="/wiki/Getica" title="Getica">Getica</a></i> (written in 551 AD),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> describes the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Veneti" title="Vistula Veneti">Veneti</a> as a "populous nation" whose dwellings begin at the sources of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> and occupy "a great expanse of land". He also describes the Veneti as the ancestors of Antes and Slaveni, two early Slavic tribes, who appeared on the Byzantine frontier in the early 6th century. Procopius wrote in 545 that "the Sclaveni and the Antae actually had a single name in the remote past; for they were both called <i><a href="/wiki/Sporoi" title="Sporoi">Sporoi</a></i> in olden times". The name <i>Sporoi</i> derives from <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> σπείρω ("I scatter grain"). He described them as barbarians, who lived under democracy, believe in one god, "the maker of lightning" (<a href="/wiki/Perun" title="Perun">Perun</a>), to whom they made sacrifice. They lived in scattered housing, and constantly changed settlement. In war, they were mainly <a href="/wiki/Foot_soldier" class="mw-redirect" title="Foot soldier">foot soldiers</a> with small shields and battle axes, lightly clothed, some entering battle naked with only genitals covered. Their language is "barbarous" (that is, not Greek), and the two tribes are alike in appearance, being tall and robust, "while their bodies and hair are neither very fair or blond, nor indeed do they incline entirely to the dark type, but they are all slightly ruddy in color. And they live a hard life, giving no heed to bodily comforts..."<sup id="cite_ref-ufl_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ufl-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Jordanes described the Sclaveni having swamps and forests for their cities.<sup id="cite_ref-jordanes1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jordanes1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Another 6th-century source refers to them living among nearly impenetrable forests, rivers, lakes, and marshes.<sup id="cite_ref-strategikon_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strategikon-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Menander_Protector" title="Menander Protector">Menander Protector</a> mentions a <a href="/wiki/Daurentius" title="Daurentius">Daurentius</a> (circa 577–579) who slew an <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avar</a> envoy of Khagan <a href="/wiki/Bayan_I" title="Bayan I">Bayan I</a> for asking the Slavs to accept the suzerainty of the Avars; Daurentius declined and is reported as saying: "Others do not conquer our land, we conquer theirs – so it shall always be for us".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurta200191–92,_315_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurta200191–92,_315-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migrations">Migrations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Migrations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg/220px-Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg/330px-Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg/440px-Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1520" data-file-height="1442" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Slavic_tribes_in_the_7th_to_9th_century.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spread of Slavic tribes from the 7th to 9th centuries AD in Europe</div></div></div>
<p>According to eastern homeland theory, prior to becoming known to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> world, <a href="/wiki/Slavic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic language">Slavic</a>-speaking tribes were part of the many multi-ethnic confederacies of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> – such as the Sarmatian, Hun and Gothic empires. The Slavs emerged from obscurity when the westward movement of Germans in the 5th and 6th centuries CE (thought to be in conjunction with the movement of peoples from Siberia and Eastern Europe: <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>) started the <a href="/wiki/Pre-modern_human_migration" title="Pre-modern human migration">great migration</a> of the Slavs, who settled the lands abandoned by Germanic tribes fleeing the Huns and their allies: westward into the country between the Oder and the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a>-<a href="/wiki/Saale" title="Saale">Saale</a> line; southward into <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a>, much of present-day <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian plain">Pannonian plain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>; and northward along the upper <a href="/wiki/Dnieper" title="Dnieper">Dnieper</a> river. It has also been suggested that some Slavs migrated with the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> and even <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclopedia_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclopedia-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Around the 6th century, Slavs appeared on <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> borders in great numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Byzantine records note that Slav numbers were so great, that grass would not regrow where the Slavs had marched through. After a military movement even the <a href="/wiki/Peloponnese" title="Peloponnese">Peloponnese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia_Minor" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Minor">Asia Minor</a> were reported to have Slavic settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> This southern movement has traditionally been seen as an invasive expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-hri_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hri-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the 6th century, Slavs had <a href="/wiki/Slavic_settlement_of_the_Eastern_Alps" title="Slavic settlement of the Eastern Alps">settled the Eastern Alps regions</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_moravia_svatopluk.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Great_moravia_svatopluk.png/220px-Great_moravia_svatopluk.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Great_moravia_svatopluk.png/330px-Great_moravia_svatopluk.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Great_moravia_svatopluk.png/440px-Great_moravia_svatopluk.png 2x" data-file-width="876" data-file-height="762" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_moravia_svatopluk.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a> was one of the first major Slavic states, 833–907 AD</div></div></div>
<p>When Slav migrations ended, their first <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">state</a> organizations appeared, each headed by a prince with a treasury and a defense force. In the 7th century, the Frankish merchant <a href="/wiki/Samo" title="Samo">Samo</a> supported the Slavs against their <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avar</a> rulers, and became the ruler of the first known Slav state in Central Europe, <a href="/wiki/Samo%27s_Empire" title="Samo&#39;s Empire">Samo's Empire</a>. This early Slavic polity probably did not outlive its founder and ruler, but it was the foundation for later <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavic</a> states on its territory. The oldest of them was <a href="/wiki/Carantania" title="Carantania">Carantania</a>; others are the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">Principality of Nitra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravian</a> principality (see under <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Balaton_Principality" class="mw-redirect" title="Balaton Principality">Balaton Principality</a>. The <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a> was founded in 681 as an alliance between the ruling <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> and the numerous <a href="/wiki/Seven_Slavic_tribes" title="Seven Slavic tribes">slavs</a> in the area, and their <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">South Slavic</a> language, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a>, became the main and official language of the empire in 864. Bulgaria was instrumental in the spread of <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Slavic literacy</a> and Christianity to the rest of the Slavic world. The expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian people">Magyars</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Germanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanization">Germanization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> gradually separated the <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a> from the <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a>. Later Slavic states, which formed in the following centuries, included the <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Kievan Rus'</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Second_Bulgarian_Empire" title="Second Bulgarian Empire">Second Bulgarian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_during_the_Piast_dynasty" title="History of Poland during the Piast dynasty">Kingdom of Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bohemia" title="Duchy of Bohemia">Duchy of Bohemia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Croatia_(medieval)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Croatia (medieval)">Kingdom of Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banate_of_Bosnia" title="Banate of Bosnia">Banate of Bosnia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Empire" title="Serbian Empire">Serbian Empire</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In late 19th century, there were only four Slavic states in the world: the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">Principality of Serbia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Montenegro" title="Principality of Montenegro">Principality of Montenegro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Bulgaria" title="Principality of Bulgaria">Principality of Bulgaria</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>, out of approximately 50 million people, about 23 million were Slavs. The Slavic peoples who were, for the most part, denied a voice in the affairs of Austria-Hungary, called for national self-determination. Because of the vastness and diversity of the territory occupied by Slavic people, there were several centers of Slavic consolidation. At the beginning of the 20th century, following the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> and the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>, several Slavic nations re-emerged and became independent, such as the <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Second Polish Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">First Czechoslovak Republic</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Kingdom of Yugoslavia</a>. After the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> and subsequent collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, additional new Slavic states emerged, such as the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, Bosnia and Herzegovina, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pan-Slavism">Pan-Slavism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Pan-Slavism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg/170px-Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg/255px-Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg/340px-Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg 2x" data-file-width="579" data-file-height="569" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Slovansky_sjezd_v_Praze_1848.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Seal from the <a href="/wiki/Prague_Slavic_Congress,_1848" title="Prague Slavic Congress, 1848">pan-Slavic Congress</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, 1848</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pan-Slavism" title="Pan-Slavism">Pan-Slavism</a>, a movement which came into prominence in the mid-19th century, emphasized the common heritage and unity of all the Slavic peoples. The main focus was in the Balkans where the South Slavs had been ruled for centuries by other empires: the Byzantine Empire, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, the Ottoman Empire, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Venice</a>. The Russian Empire used Pan-Slavism as a political tool;<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> as did the Soviet Union, which gained political-military influence and control over most Slavic-majority nations between 1939 and 1948 and retained a hegemonic role until the period 1989–1991.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Slavic_languages" title="History of the Slavic languages">History of the Slavic languages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic languages</a></div>

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG/170px-Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG" decoding="async" width="170" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG/255px-Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG/340px-Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG 2x" data-file-width="815" data-file-height="828" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_eslavas_orientales.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>East Slavic languages</b>. <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; <div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG/170px-Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG" decoding="async" width="170" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG/255px-Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG/340px-Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="544" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_eslavas_occidentales.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>West Slavic languages</b>.<br /> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Polish</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A52A2A; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Kashubian</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF6347; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Silesian</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8B008B; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Polabian †</div> <br /> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF00FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Lower Sorbian</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #EE82EE; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Upper Sorbian</div> <br /> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF8C00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Czech</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFD700; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Slovak</div></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Slavic language">Proto-Slavic</a>, the supposed ancestor language of all Slavic languages, is a descendant of common <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">Proto-Indo-European</a>, via a <a href="/wiki/Proto-Balto-Slavic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Balto-Slavic">Balto-Slavic stage</a> in which it developed numerous lexical and morphophonological isoglosses with the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltic language">Baltic languages</a>. In the framework of the <a href="/wiki/Kurgan_hypothesis" title="Kurgan hypothesis">Kurgan hypothesis</a>, "the Indo-Europeans who remained after the migrations [from the steppe] became speakers of Balto-Slavic".<sup id="cite_ref-kortlandt_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kortlandt-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Proto-Slavic is defined as the last stage of the language preceding the geographical split of the historical <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic languages</a>. That language was uniform, and on the basis of borrowings from foreign languages and Slavic borrowings into other languages, cannot be said to have any recognizable dialects – this suggests that there was, at one time, a relatively small <a href="/wiki/Slavic_urheimat" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic urheimat">Proto-Slavic homeland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kortlandt5_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kortlandt5-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Slavic linguistic unity was to some extent visible as late as <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">Old Church Slavonic</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Old_Bulgarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Bulgarian">Old Bulgarian</a>) manuscripts which, though based on local Slavic speech of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, could still serve the purpose of the first common Slavic literary language.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavic_studies" title="Slavic studies">Slavic studies</a> began as an almost exclusively linguistic and philological enterprise. As early as 1833, Slavic languages were recognized as Indo-European.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">Standardised</a> Slavic languages that have official status in at least one country are: <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_language" title="Bosnian language">Bosnian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">Macedonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a>.
</p><p>The alphabets used for Slavic languages are frequently connected to the dominant religion among the respective ethnic groups. Orthodox Christians use the <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic alphabet</a> while Roman Catholics use the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>; the Bosniaks, who are Muslim, also use the Latin alphabet. Additionally, some <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholics</a> and Roman Catholics use the Cyrillic alphabet. <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">Serbian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_language" title="Montenegrin language">Montenegrin</a> use both the Cyrillic and Latin alphabets. There is also a Latin script to write in <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Latin_alphabet" title="Belarusian Latin alphabet">Łacinka</a>.
</p>

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:rgb(220,245,220);padding-left:0.4em;text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Indo-European_studies" title="Indo-European studies">Indo-European studies</a></div><div class="NavContent hlist" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center">
<dl><dt><i>Scholars</i></dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Marija_Gimbutas" title="Marija Gimbutas">Marija Gimbutas</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J._P._Mallory" title="J. P. Mallory">J. P. Mallory</a></li></ul>
<dl><dt><i>Institutes</i></dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Studies_in_Indo-European" title="Copenhagen Studies in Indo-European">Copenhagen Studies in Indo-European</a></li></ul>
<dl><dt><i>Publications</i></dt></dl>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Encyclopedia_of_Indo-European_Culture" title="Encyclopedia of Indo-European Culture">Encyclopedia of Indo-European Culture</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Horse,_the_Wheel_and_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="The Horse, the Wheel and Language">The Horse, the Wheel and Language</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Indo-European_Studies" title="Journal of Indo-European Studies">Journal of Indo-European Studies</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Indogermanisches_etymologisches_W%C3%B6rterbuch" title="Indogermanisches etymologisches Wörterbuch">Indogermanisches etymologisches Wörterbuch</a></i></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Indo-European_Etymological_Dictionary" title="Indo-European Etymological Dictionary">Indo-European Etymological Dictionary</a></i></li></ul></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Indo-European_topics" title="Template:Indo-European topics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Indo-European_topics" title="Template talk:Indo-European topics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Indo-European_topics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Slavs are customarily divided along geographical lines into three major subgroups: <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a>, each with a different and a diverse background based on unique history, religion and culture of particular Slavic groups within them. Apart from prehistorical archaeological cultures, the subgroups have had notable cultural contact with non-Slavic <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze</a>- and <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> civilisations. Modern Slavic nations and ethnic groups are considerably diverse both genetically and culturally, and relations between them – even within the individual ethnic groups themselves – are varied, ranging from a sense of connection to mutual feelings of hostility.<sup id="cite_ref-Psychology_Press_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Psychology_Press-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (March 2017)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a> originate from early Slavic tribes which settled in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> after the <a href="/wiki/East_Germanic_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="East Germanic tribes">East Germanic tribes</a> had left this area during the <a href="/wiki/Migration_period" class="mw-redirect" title="Migration period">migration period</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> They are noted as having mixed with <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germanics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> (particularly the <a href="/wiki/Boii" title="Boii">Boii</a>), <a href="/wiki/Old_Prussians" title="Old Prussians">Old Prussians</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Pannonian Avars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stocki1950_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stocki1950-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The West Slavs came under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> (Latin) and of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a> have origins in early Slavic tribes who mixed and contacted with <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_peoples" title="Finno-Ugric peoples">Finno-Ugric peoples</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balts" title="Balts">Balts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ZickelDivision1991_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZickelDivision1991-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Their early Slavic component, <a href="/wiki/Antes_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Antes people">Antes</a>, mixed or absorbed <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranians</a>, and later received influence from the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVlasto1970237_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVlasto1970237-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The East Slavs trace their national origins to the tribal unions of <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">Kievan Rus'</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_Khaganate" title="Rus&#39; Khaganate">Rus' Khaganate</a>, beginning in the 10th century. They came particularly under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a> from most of the region have origins in early Slavic tribes who mixed with the local Proto-Balkanic tribes (<a href="/wiki/Illyrian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Illyrian tribes">Illyrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dacian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Dacian tribes">Dacian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thracian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Thracian tribes">Thracian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paeonian_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Paeonian tribes">Paeonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Hellenic tribes">Hellenic tribes</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic tribes">Celtic tribes</a> (particularly the <a href="/wiki/Scordisci" title="Scordisci">Scordisci</a>), as well as with Romans (and the Romanized remnants of the former groups), and also with remnants of temporarily settled invading East Germanic, Asiatic or Caucasian tribes such as <a href="/wiki/Gepids" title="Gepids">Gepids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" class="mw-redirect" title="Avars (Carpathians)">Avars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The original inhabitants of present-day Slovenia and continental Croatia have origins in early Slavic tribes who mixed with Romans and romanized Celtic and Illyrian people as well as with Avars and Germanic peoples (Lombards and East Goths). The South Slavs (except the Slovenes and Croats) came under the cultural sphere of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a> (Byzantine Empire), of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, while the Slovenes and the Croats were influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> (Latin) and thus by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> in a similar fashion to that of the West Slavs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%22Swiatowid_(cult_statue)%22,_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/%22Swiatowid_%28cult_statue%29%22%2C_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg/170px-%22Swiatowid_%28cult_statue%29%22%2C_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/%22Swiatowid_%28cult_statue%29%22%2C_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg/255px-%22Swiatowid_%28cult_statue%29%22%2C_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/%22Swiatowid_%28cult_statue%29%22%2C_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg/340px-%22Swiatowid_%28cult_statue%29%22%2C_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1546" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%22Swiatowid_(cult_statue)%22,_Krak%C3%B3w_2013.2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "Zbruch Idol" preserved at <a href="/wiki/Krakow" class="mw-redirect" title="Krakow">Krakow</a> Archaeological Museum</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Slavic_mythology" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic mythology">Slavic mythology</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Slavic_mythology" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic mythology">pagan Slavic</a> populations <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_the_Slavs" title="Christianization of the Slavs">were Christianized</a> between the 7th and 12th centuries. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a> is predominant among East and South Slavs, while <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> is predominant among West Slavs and some western <a href="/wiki/South_Slavs" title="South Slavs">South Slavs</a>. The religious borders are largely comparable to the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">East–West Schism</a> which began in the 11th century.
</p><p>The majority of contemporary Slavic populations who profess a religion are Orthodox, followed by Catholic, while a small minority are <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>. There are minor <a href="/wiki/Slavic_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic Muslims">Slavic Muslim</a> groups. Religious delineations by nationality can be very sharp; usually in the Slavic ethnic groups the vast majority of religious people share the same religion. Some Slavs are <a href="/wiki/Atheist" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheist">atheist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Agnostic" class="mw-redirect" title="Agnostic">agnostic</a>: in the <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Religion in the Czech Republic">Czech Republic 20% were atheists</a> according to a 2012 poll.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_non-Slavic_people">Relations with non-Slavic people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Relations with non-Slavic people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Slavic_piracy" title="Baltic Slavic piracy">Baltic Slavic piracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Narentines" title="Narentines">Narentines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkans_about_680_A.D.,_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Balkans_about_680_A.D.%2C_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png/170px-Balkans_about_680_A.D.%2C_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Balkans_about_680_A.D.%2C_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png/255px-Balkans_about_680_A.D.%2C_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Balkans_about_680_A.D.%2C_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png/340px-Balkans_about_680_A.D.%2C_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png 2x" data-file-width="1716" data-file-height="2496" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Balkans_about_680_A.D.,_foundation_of_the_First_Bulgarian_Empire.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> were a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> semi-nomadic warrior tribe that became Slavicized in the 7th century AD</div></div></div>
<p>Throughout their history, Slavs came into contact with non-Slavic groups. In the postulated homeland region (present-day <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>), they had contacts with the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatians</a> and the Germanic <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>. After their subsequent spread, the Slavs began assimilating non-Slavic peoples. For example, in the Balkans, there were <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Southeastern_Europe" title="Prehistory of Southeastern Europe">Paleo-Balkan</a> peoples, such as Romanized and Hellenized (<a href="/wiki/Jire%C4%8Dek_Line" title="Jireček Line">Jireček Line</a>) <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">Illyrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">Thracians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dacians" title="Dacians">Dacians</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Scordisci" title="Scordisci">Scordisci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serdi" title="Serdi">Serdi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Because Slavs were so numerous, most indigenous populations of the Balkans were Slavicized. Thracians and Illyrians vanished as defined ethnic groups in this period. Exceptions are Greece, where Slavs were Hellenized because Greeks were more numerous (aided by more Greeks returning to Greece in the 9th century and by the church and administration),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFine199141_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFine199141-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, where Slavs settled en route to present-day Greece, North Macedonia, Bulgaria and <a href="/wiki/East_Thrace" title="East Thrace">East Thrace</a> but assimilated, and the modern <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanian</a> nation which claims descent from Illyrians.
</p><p>Ruling status of <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> and their control of land cast the nominal legacy of the <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgarian country and people</a> onto future generations, but Bulgars were gradually also Slavicized into the present day South Slavic ethnic group known as <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>. The Romance speakers within the fortified Dalmatian cities retained their culture and language for a long time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFine199135_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFine199135-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Dalmatian Romance was spoken until the high Middle Ages, but, they too were eventually assimilated into the body of Slavs.
</p><p>In the Western Balkans, South Slavs and Germanic <a href="/wiki/Gepids" title="Gepids">Gepids</a> intermarried with invaders, eventually producing a Slavicized population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In Central Europe, the West Slavs intermixed with <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">Hungarian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> peoples, while in Eastern Europe the East Slavs had encountered <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Finns" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltic Finns">Finnic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Varangians" title="Varangians">Scandinavian peoples</a>. Scandinavians (<a href="/wiki/Varangians" title="Varangians">Varangians</a>) and Finnic peoples were involved in the <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus&#39;">early formation of the Rus' state</a> but were completely Slavicized after a century. Some <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_peoples" title="Finno-Ugric peoples">Finno-Ugric</a> tribes in the north were also absorbed into the expanding Rus population.<sup id="cite_ref-Balanovsky20082_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balanovsky20082-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In the 11th and 12th centuries, constant incursions by nomadic <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> tribes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Kipchaks" title="Kipchaks">Kipchak</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pecheneg" class="mw-redirect" title="Pecheneg">Pecheneg</a>, caused a massive migration of East Slavic populations to the safer, heavily forested regions of the north.<sup id="cite_ref-The_course_of_the_Russian_history2_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_course_of_the_Russian_history2-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In the Middle Ages, groups of <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxon</a> ore miners settled in medieval <a href="/wiki/Bosnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bosnia">Bosnia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, where they were Slavicized.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Saqaliba" title="Saqaliba">Saqaliba</a></i> refers to the Slavic <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenaries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a> in the medieval Arab world in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a>. Saqaliba served as caliph's guards.<sup id="cite_ref-fordham2_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fordham2-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In the 12th century, <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Slavic_piracy" title="Baltic Slavic piracy">Slavic piracy in the Baltics</a> increased.  The <a href="/wiki/Wendish_Crusade" title="Wendish Crusade">Wendish Crusade</a> was started against the Polabian Slavs in 1147, as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Crusades" title="Northern Crusades">Northern Crusades</a>. The pagan chief of the Slavic <a href="/wiki/Obotrites" title="Obotrites">Obodrite</a> tribes, <a href="/wiki/Niklot" title="Niklot">Niklot</a>, began his open resistance when <a href="/wiki/Lothar_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Lothar III">Lothar III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>, invaded Slavic lands. In August 1160 Niklot was killed, and German colonization (<i><a href="/wiki/Ostsiedlung" title="Ostsiedlung">Ostsiedlung</a></i>) of the Elbe-Oder region began. In <a href="/wiki/Hanoverian_Wendland" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanoverian Wendland">Hanoverian Wendland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mecklenburg-Vorpommern" title="Mecklenburg-Vorpommern">Mecklenburg-Vorpommern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">Lusatia</a>, invaders started <a href="/wiki/Germanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanization">germanization</a>. Early forms of germanization were described by German monks: <a href="/wiki/Helmold" title="Helmold">Helmold</a> in the manuscript <i><a href="/wiki/Chronicon_Slavorum" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronicon Slavorum">Chronicon Slavorum</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_of_Bremen" title="Adam of Bremen">Adam of Bremen</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Gesta_Hammaburgensis_ecclesiae_pontificum" title="Gesta Hammaburgensis ecclesiae pontificum">Gesta Hammaburgensis ecclesiae pontificum</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-britannica2_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica2-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Polabian_language" title="Polabian language">Polabian language</a> survived until the beginning of the 19th century in what is now the German state of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Saxony" title="Lower Saxony">Lower Saxony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica42_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica42-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Germany">Eastern Germany</a>, around 20% of Germans have historic Slavic paternal ancestry, as revealed in Y-DNA testing.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, in Germany, around 20% of the foreign surnames are of Slavic origin.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Cossacks" title="History of the Cossacks">Cossacks</a>, although Slavic-speaking and practicing <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a>, came from a mix of ethnic backgrounds, including <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turks</a>. Many early members of the <a href="/wiki/Terek_Cossacks" title="Terek Cossacks">Terek Cossacks</a> were <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gorals" title="Gorals">Gorals</a> of southern <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> are partially descended from Romance-speaking <a href="/wiki/Vlachs" title="Vlachs">Vlachs</a>, who migrated into the region from the 14th to 17th centuries and were absorbed into the local population. The population of <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Wallachia" title="Moravian Wallachia">Moravian Wallachia</a> also descended from the Vlachs. Conversely, some Slavs were assimilated into other populations. Although the majority continued towards Southeast Europe, attracted by the riches of the area that became the state of <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgaria</a>, a few remained in the Carpathian Basin in Central Europe, and were assimilated into the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian people">Magyar</a> people. Numerous river and other place names in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Romania" title="History of Romania">Romania</a> have Slavic origin.<sup id="cite_ref-alexandru2_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexandru2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (April 2015)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Slavs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are an estimated 360 million Slavs worldwide.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png/220px-Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png/330px-Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png/440px-Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png 2x" data-file-width="1749" data-file-height="1740" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Slavic_ancestry_in_the_USA_and_Canada.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Slavs in the US and Canada by area: <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block;
